     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satellite_facilities">Satellite facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Satellite facilities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university also maintains a number of facilities apart from its main campus. The <a href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center" class="mw-redirect">J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center</a> also has a teaching hospital located at <a href="/wiki/UF_Health_at_Jacksonville" title="UF Health at Jacksonville">UF Health at Jacksonville</a>, which serves as the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a> campus for the University's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Medicine-Jacksonville" title="University of Florida College of Medicine-Jacksonville">College of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Nursing" title="University of Florida College of Nursing">College of Nursing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Florida College of Pharmacy">College of Pharmacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jaxshands_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaxshands-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> A number of residencies are also offered at this facility.<sup id="cite_ref-jaxshands_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jaxshands-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The University's College of Pharmacy also maintains campuses in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Dentistry maintains clinics in <a href="/wiki/Hialeah,_Florida" title="Hialeah, Florida">Hialeah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naples,_Florida" title="Naples, Florida">Naples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg,_Florida" title="St. Petersburg, Florida">St. Petersburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's <a href="/wiki/Warrington_College_of_Business" title="Warrington College of Business" class="mw-redirect">Warrington College of Business</a> established programs in <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a> in 2004, and recently built a 6,100-square-foot (570&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) facility in <a href="/wiki/Sunrise,_Florida" title="Sunrise, Florida">Sunrise, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Food_and_Agricultural_Sciences" title="Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences">Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences</a> has <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_extension_service" title="Cooperative extension service" class="mw-redirect">extensions</a> in each of the 67 counties in Florida, and 13 research and education centers with a total of 19 locations throughout the state.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, the university established the Beijing Center for International Studies in <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> that offers research facilities, offices, and degree opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sid_Martin_Biotechnology_Incubator" title="Sid Martin Biotechnology Incubator">Sid Martin Biotechnology Incubator</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/220px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/330px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG/440px-UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UF_Cancer_Genetics_Complex.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Cancer_and_Genetics_Research_Complex" title="University of Florida Cancer and Genetics Research Complex">University of Florida Cancer and Genetics Research Complex</a> is one of several research facilities at the university
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida is one of the largest research universities in the nation. According to a 2011 study by UF's <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Food_and_Agricultural_Sciences" title="Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences">Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences</a>, the university contributed $8.76 billion to Florida's economy and was responsible for over 100,000 jobs in the 2009–2010 fiscal year.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The Milken Institute named UF one of the top-five U.S. institutions in the transfer of <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> research to the marketplace (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> Some 50 biotechnology companies have resulted from faculty research programs. UF consistently ranks among the top-10 universities in licensing.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Royalty and licensing income includes the glaucoma drug <a href="/wiki/Trusopt" title="Trusopt" class="mw-redirect">Trusopt</a>, the sports drink <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a>, and the Sentricon <a href="/wiki/Termite" title="Termite">termite</a> elimination system. The Institute of Food and Agricultural Sciences is ranked #1 <sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> by the NSF in Research and Development; its current Vice President is Dr. Larry Arrington. UF currently ranks seventh among all private &amp; public universities for the total number of patents awarded for 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Florida was awarded $678 million in total research expenditures, more than all the other Florida universities combined, in sponsored research in 2009-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Research includes diverse areas such as health-care and citrus production (the world's largest citrus research center). In 2002, UF began leading six other universities under a $15 million <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> grant to work on a variety of space-related research during a five-year period.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> UF has a partnership with Spain that helped to create the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Telescopio_Canarias" title="Gran Telescopio Canarias">world's largest single-aperture optical telescope</a> in the Canary Islands (the total cost was $93 million).<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Plans are also under way for the University of Florida to construct a new 50,000-square-foot (4,600&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) research facility in collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Burnham_Institute_for_Medical_Research" title="Burnham Institute for Medical Research" class="mw-redirect">Burnham Institute for Medical Research</a> that will ultimately be located in the center of <a href="/wiki/UCF" title="UCF" class="mw-redirect">UCF</a>'s Health Sciences Campus in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Research will include the areas of diabetes, aging, genetics and cancer.</p> 
     <p>The University of Florida has made great strides in the space sciences over the last decade.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The Astronomy Department's focus on the development of image-detection devices has led to increases in funding, telescope time, and significant scholarly achievements. Faculty members in organic chemistry have made notable discoveries in astrobiology, while faculty members in physics have participated actively in the <a href="/wiki/Laser_Interferometer_Gravitational-Wave_Observatory" title="Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory" class="mw-redirect">Laser Interferometer Gravitational-Wave Observatory</a> project, the largest and most ambitious project ever funded by the NSF.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> Through the Department of Mechanical and Aerospace Engineering, the University of Florida is the lead institution on the NASA University Research, Engineering, and Technology Institute (URETI) for Future Space Transport project to develop the next generation space shuttle.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, UF is also doing some innovative Diabetes Research In a statewide screening program, that has been sponsored by a $10 million grant from the <a href="/wiki/American_Diabetes_Association" title="American Diabetes Association">American Diabetes Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Florida also houses one of the world's leading lightning research teams.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Also UF scientists have started up a biofuels pilot plant that has been specifically designed to test ethanol-producing technology.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> UF is also host to a <a href="/wiki/UF_Training_Reactor" title="UF Training Reactor">nuclear research reactor</a> which is known for its Neutron Activation Analysis Laboratory.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the University of Florida is the first American university to receive a <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> grant to house a <a href="/wiki/Jean_Monnet" title="Jean Monnet">Jean Monnet</a> Centre of Excellence.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UF has more than $750 million in new research facilities recently completed or under construction, including the Nanoscale Research Facility, the Pathogens Research Facility and the Biomedical Sciences Building.<sup id="cite_ref-ufl_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ufl-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, Innovation Square, a 24/7 live/work/play research environment being developed along Southwest Second Avenue between the University of Florida campus and downtown Gainesville, recently broke ground and plans to open next fall. UF’s Office of Technology Licensing will relocate to Innovation Square, joining Florida Innovation Hub, a business “super-incubator” designed to promote the development of new high-tech companies based on UF research. Companies will be recruited from around the country to locate at Innovation Square, venture capitalists will want to be part of the project and startup companies will blossom. Innovation Square also will include retail space, restaurants and local businesses, as well as residential space for people to live.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_International_Center_for_Lightning_Research_and_Testing">The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Florida has more <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> than any other state in the U.S. The University of Florida houses one of the world's leading international lightning research teams. <b>The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing</b> (ICLRT) are run by the University of Florida at the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Blanding" title="Camp Blanding">Camp Blanding</a> Florida Army National Guard Base.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The ICLRT Center occupies over 100 acre (40 ha) at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Blanding" title="Camp Blanding">Camp Blanding</a>, located about 25 miles (45&nbsp;km) north-east of <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville, Florida</a>. One of their primary research tools is lightning initiation from overhead thunderclouds using the triggered lightning rocket-and-wire technique. Small sounding rockets connected to long copper wires are fired into likely <a href="/wiki/Lightning_storm" title="Lightning storm" class="mw-redirect">lightning storm</a> <a href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus" title="Cumulonimbus" class="mw-redirect">cumulonimbus</a> clouds. When the rocket or its wire is struck by lightning, the passing of the high current lightning strike down the wire vaporizes it as it as lightning travels to the ground. Undergraduate and graduate Research in the Department of Electrical and Computer Engineering UF Lightning Research Group is used to increase new fundamental knowledge about lightning based phenomena and teach students.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_Science_Center">Health Science Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health Science Center">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center" class="mw-redirect">J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center" class="mw-redirect">J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center</a> (HSC) has facilities in <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville</a>. The HSC comprises the university's Colleges of Dentistry, Medicine, Nursing, Pharmacy, Public Health &amp; Health Professions and Veterinary Medicine. The Health Science Center is the only academic health center in the United States with six health-related colleges located on a single, contiguous campus.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The facility was named after the 4th President of the University of Florida <a href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller,_Sr." title="J. Hillis Miller, Sr.">J. Hillis Miller, Sr.</a>. In all the HSC generates over $280 million in total research expenditures for the 2008-2009 fiscal year. The Health Science Center focus on blindness, hypertension and smoking cessation.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Health Science Center is also affiliated with <a href="/wiki/UF_Health_Shands_Hospital" title="UF Health Shands Hospital">UF Health Shands Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/UF_Health_Jacksonville" title="UF Health Jacksonville" class="mw-redirect">UF Health Jacksonville</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Veterans_Affairs" title="United States Department of Veterans Affairs">Veterans Affairs</a> hospitals in Gainesville and North Florida/South Georgia. In all 6,159 total students are enrolled in all six of the colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Currently being constructed is a new <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Cancer_Hospital" title="University of Florida Cancer Hospital">University of Florida Cancer Hospital</a> which can be found on Archer road in <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a>. The facility is estimated to cost $388 million, and is expected to be 500,000 square feet (46,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/McKnight_Brain_Institute" title="McKnight Brain Institute">McKnight Brain Institute</a> is also part of the Health Science Center and is the most comprehensive program of its kind in the world. The Institute comprises 300 faculty members from 10 colleges, and 51 departments campus-wide.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Florida is a winner of the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a> Clinical and Translational Science Award and member of the prestigious NIH national consortium of medical research institutions.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnership_with_Moffitt_Center">Partnership with Moffitt Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Partnership with Moffitt Center">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG/250px-Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG" width="250" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG/375px-Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c5/Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG/500px-Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Moffitt_Cancer_Center_viewed_from_east.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/H._Lee_Moffitt_Cancer_Center_%26_Research_Institute" title="H. Lee Moffitt Cancer Center &amp; Research Institute">Moffitt Cancer Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In January 2008 the University of Florida, <a href="/wiki/H._Lee_Moffitt_Cancer_Center_%26_Research_Institute" title="H. Lee Moffitt Cancer Center &amp; Research Institute">H. Lee Moffitt Cancer Center &amp; Research Institute</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shands_at_the_University_of_Florida" title="Shands at the University of Florida" class="mw-redirect">Shands at the University of Florida</a> formed a partnership to develop world-class programs in cancer care, research and prevention. The partnership, will extend Moffitt's innovative model of comprehensive patient care to UF Health cancer programs.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Participation_in_the_Large_Hadron_Collider">Participation in the Large Hadron Collider</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Participation in the Large Hadron Collider">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>A team of UF physicists has a leading role in one of the two major experiments planned for the <a href="/wiki/Large_Hadron_Collider" title="Large Hadron Collider">Large Hadron Collider</a>, a 17-mile (27&nbsp;km)-long, $5 billion, super-cooled underground tunnel outside Geneva, Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> More than 30 UF physicists, postdoctoral associates, graduate students and now undergraduates are involved in the collider's <a href="/wiki/Compact_Muon_Solenoid" title="Compact Muon Solenoid">Compact Muon Solenoid</a> (CMS) experiment, one of its two major experiments. About 10 are stationed in Geneva. The group is the largest from any university in the U.S. to participate in the CMS experiment. The UF team designed and oversaw development of a major detector within the CMS. The detector, the Muon system, is intended to capture subatomic particles called muons, which are heavier cousins of electrons. Among other efforts, UF scientists analyzed about 100 of the 400 detector chambers placed within the Muon system to be sure they were functioning properly. The bulk of the UF research was funded by the U.S. Department of Energy.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnership_with_Zhejiang_University">Partnership with Zhejiang University</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Partnership with Zhejiang University">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In July 2008, the University of Florida teamed up with the <a href="/wiki/Zhejiang_University" title="Zhejiang University">Zhejiang University</a> to research sustainable solutions to the Earth's energy issues. Overall a Joint Research Center of Clean Sustainable Energy among the Florida Institute for Sustainable Energy, at UF, and the State Key Lab of Clean Energy Utilization and the Institute for Thermal Power Engineering, at Zhejiang University will collaborate to work on this pressing issue.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="SECU:_SEC_Academic_Initiative">SECU: SEC Academic Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: SECU: SEC Academic Initiative">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The University of Florida is a member of the SEC Academic Consortium. Now renamed the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#The_Formation_of_SECU_and_SEC_Academic_Network" title="Southeastern Conference">SECU</a>, the initiative was a collaborative endeavor designed to promote research, scholarship and achievement amongst the member universities in the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_conference" title="Southeastern conference" class="mw-redirect">Southeastern conference</a>. Along with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">University of Georgia</a>, University of Florida, <a href="/wiki/Vanderbilt_University" title="Vanderbilt University">Vanderbilt University</a> and other SEC institutions, SECU formed its mission to serve as a means to bolster collaborative academic endeavors of <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference#Member_universities" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference universities</a>. Its goals include highlighting the endeavors and achievements of SEC <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(academic_staff)" title="Faculty (academic staff)">faculty</a>, students and its universities and advancing the academic reputation of SEC universities.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2013, the University of Florida participated in the SEC Symposium in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia" class="mw-redirect">Atlanta, Georgia</a> which was organized and led by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">University of Georgia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia#UGA_Bioenergy_Systems_Research_Institute" title="University of Georgia">UGA Bioenergy Systems Research Institute</a>. The topic of the Symposium was titled, the &quot;Impact of the Southeast in the World's Renewable Energy Future.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/220px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/330px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/da/UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG/440px-UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UFHistoricBuildingSmathersLibraryEastInteriorSpecialCollectionsRoom.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Smathers Library, first opened in 1926, is the oldest library at the university
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/George_A._Smathers_Libraries" title="George A. Smathers Libraries">George A. Smathers Libraries</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida's <a href="/wiki/George_A._Smathers_Libraries" title="George A. Smathers Libraries">George A. Smathers Libraries</a>, is one of the largest university library systems in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, the University of Florida has ten libraries, and over 5.3 million volumes of books and journals and 7 million microfilms.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Collections cover virtually all disciplines and include a wide array of formats – from books and journals to manuscripts, maps, and recorded music. Increasingly collections are digital and are accessible on the Internet via the library web page or the library catalog.</p> 
     <p>The numerous libraries provide primary support to all academic programs except those served by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.library.health.ufl.edu/">Health Science Center Library</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lawton_Chiles_Legal_Information_Center" title="Lawton Chiles Legal Information Center">Lawton Chiles Legal Information Center</a>. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Library_West" title="University of Florida Library West">Library West</a> went through a $30 million dollar renovation that doubled capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> This facility is now better equipped to handle the information technology necessities that students need to complete their studies. Such progress is represented by its state-of-the-art Information Commons,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> which offers production studios, digital media computing areas, and a presentation area.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_buildings" title="List of University of Florida buildings">List of University of Florida buildings</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In total the University of Florida campus encompasses over 2,000 acres (8.1&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>). The campus is home to many notable structures, such as <a href="/wiki/Century_Tower_(University_of_Florida)" title="Century Tower (University of Florida)">Century Tower</a>, a 157-foot (48&nbsp;m) tall <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> tower in the center of the historic district. Other notable facilities include the <a href="/wiki/J._Hillis_Miller_Health_Science_Center" title="J. Hillis Miller Health Science Center" class="mw-redirect">Health Science Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Union">Reitz Student Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Library_East_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Library East (Gainesville, Florida)">Smathers Library</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Harn Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Hub_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="The Hub (Gainesville, Florida)">The Hub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg/150px-Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg/225px-Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg/300px-Gville_UF_Floyd03.jpg 2x" /></a>

        <a href="/wiki/Griffin-Floyd_Hall" title="Griffin-Floyd Hall">Griffin-Floyd Hall</a>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_sites">Historic sites</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Historic sites">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>A number of the University of Florida's buildings are historically significant. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Campus_Historic_District" title="University of Florida Campus Historic District">University of Florida Campus Historic District</a> comprises 19 buildings and encompasses approximately 650 acres (2.6&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-OCHP_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCHP-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Two buildings outside the historic district, the <a href="/wiki/Old_WRUF_Radio_Station" title="Old WRUF Radio Station">old WRUF radio station</a> (now the university police station) and <a href="/wiki/Norman_Hall_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Norman Hall (Gainesville, Florida)">Norman Hall</a> (formerly the P. K. Yonge Laboratory School), are also listed on the historic register.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> The buildings listed on the U.S. National Register of Historic Places for their architectural or historic significance are:</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_.26_sororities">Fraternities &amp; sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Fraternities &amp; sororities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Approximately 5,200 undergraduate students (or approximately 15%) are members of either a sorority or fraternity.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sorority" title="Sorority" class="mw-redirect">Sorority</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">Fraternity</a> Affairs (formerly known as Greek Life) at the University of Florida is separated into four divisions: <a href="/wiki/North-American_Interfraternity_Conference" title="North-American Interfraternity Conference">Interfraternity Council</a> (IFC), <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> (NPC), <a href="/wiki/National_Multicultural_Greek_Council" title="National Multicultural Greek Council">Multicultural Greek Council</a> (MGC), and the <a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> (NPHC). The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Omega" title="Order of Omega">Order of Omega</a> has a chapter at the university.</p> 
     <p>The Interfraternity Council (IFC) comprises 25 fraternities, and the Panhellenic Council is made up of 16 sororities. Some of the fraternity chapters on campus are older than the university itself, with the first chapters being chartered in 1884 and founded on the campus of one of the university's predecessor institutions in Lake City.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Multicultural Greek Council consists of 12 cultural organizations (<a href="/wiki/Latino" title="Latino" class="mw-redirect">Latino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a>, etc.), seven fraternities and five sororities. The National Pan-Hellenic Council comprises nine historically black organizations, five fraternities and four sororities.</p> 
     <p>There are now also four university recognized organizations for Christian students, <a href="/wiki/Beta_Upsilon_Chi" title="Beta Upsilon Chi">Beta Upsilon Chi</a> and Kappa Phi Epsilon fraternities as well as <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Lambda" title="Sigma Phi Lambda">Sigma Phi Lambda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_sorority" title="Christian sorority">Theta Alpha</a> sororities.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF_GreekBuildings.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/UF_GreekBuildings.jpg/220px-UF_GreekBuildings.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/UF_GreekBuildings.jpg/330px-UF_GreekBuildings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/UF_GreekBuildings.jpg/440px-UF_GreekBuildings.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption">

        </div> Sororities on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps">Reserve Officer Training Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Reserve Officer Training Corps">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_ROTC" title="University of Florida ROTC">University of Florida ROTC</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps" title="Reserve Officer Training Corps" class="mw-redirect">Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> is the official <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officer</a> training and commissioning program at the University of Florida. Officially founded in 1905, it is one of the oldest such programs in the nation.</p> 
     <p>The Reserve Officer Training Corps offers commissions for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>. The unit is one of the oldest in the nation, and is currently located at <a href="/wiki/Van_Fleet_Hall_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Van Fleet Hall (Gainesville, Florida)">Van Fleet Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Reserve Officer Training Corps at the University of Florida offers training in the military sciences to students who desire to perform military service after they graduate. The Departments of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Army" title="U.S. Army" class="mw-redirect">Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force" class="mw-redirect">Air Force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" title="U.S. Navy" class="mw-redirect">Navy</a> each maintain a Reserve Officers Training Corps and each individual department has a full staff of military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_student_housing" title="University of Florida student housing">University of Florida student housing</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida provides over 9,200 students with housing in residence halls and complexes on the eastern and western sides of campus.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> Facilities vary in the cost of rent and privacy. Housing plans also offer students access to dining facilities. The university also provides housing to a number of graduate students and their families.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recreation">Recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Recreation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/275px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG" width="275" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/413px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG/550px-UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UF-RecreationalAreaAtBroward.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Recreational complex near Broward Hall.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Many recreational activities available for students include indoor and outdoor sports, outdoor courts and playing fields on campus, in the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bostic_Golf_Course" title="Mark Bostic Golf Course" class="mw-redirect">University Golf Course</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plaza_of_the_Americas_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Plaza of the Americas (Gainesville, Florida)">Plaza of the Americas</a>, the Student Recreation and Fitness Center, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Southwest_Recreation_Center" title="University of Florida Southwest Recreation Center">Southwest Recreation Center</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Gymnasium" title="University of Florida Gymnasium" class="mw-redirect">Florida Gymnasium</a> for indoor sports.<sup id="cite_ref-FU_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FU-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Florida offers intramural and club sports ranging from archery to weightlifting.<sup id="cite_ref-FU_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FU-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Near the campus are many recreational lakes and rivers, including university-owned <a href="/wiki/Lake_Alice_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Lake Alice (Gainesville, Florida)">Lake Alice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FU_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FU-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, student have access to the <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Union">J. Wayne Reitz Union</a> which is equipped with a <a href="/wiki/Bowling" title="Bowling">bowling alley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billiard_table" title="Billiard table">pool tables</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Video_arcade" title="Video arcade" class="mw-redirect">arcade</a>, and numerous other activities. South of Gainesville is <a href="/wiki/Paynes_Prairie" title="Paynes Prairie">Lake Wauburg</a>, which also provides recreational activities for students, faculty, and staff. To the northwest of campus is the <a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_Millhopper_Geological_State_Park" title="Devil's Millhopper Geological State Park">Devil's Millhopper Geological State Park</a>.</p> 
     <p>The campus also contains open spaces, small ponds, picnic areas, shady nooks and an 81-acre (330,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) wildlife sanctuary that provide opportunities to enjoy Florida's year-round sunshine activity life.<sup id="cite_ref-FU_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FU-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Lastly, the University of Florida has more than eight hundred organizations and clubs for students to join.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> They range from cultural and athletic to subjects pertaining to philanthropy. Some of the most popular organizations are <a href="/wiki/Florida_Blue_Key" title="Florida Blue Key">Florida Blue Key</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Strike_Force" title="Theatre Strike Force">Theatre Strike Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/The_Pride_of_the_Sunshine" title="The Pride of the Sunshine">Marching Band</a>, Florida Competitive Cheerleading, <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_dazzlers" title="Florida Gators dazzlers" class="mw-redirect">Dazzlers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gatorettes" title="Gatorettes" class="mw-redirect">Gatorettes</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Hillel" title="University of Florida Hillel">Hillel at UF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gator_Growl" title="Gator Growl">Gator Growl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Black_%26_Journalists_(PB%26J)" title="Progressive Black &amp; Journalists (PB&amp;J)" class="mw-redirect">Progressive Black Journalists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miss_University_of_Florida" title="Miss University of Florida">Miss University of Florida</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/ACCENT_Speakers_Bureau" title="ACCENT Speakers Bureau">Speakers Bureau</a>. If students wish they can create their own registered <a href="/wiki/Student_organization" title="Student organization" class="mw-redirect">student organization</a> if the current interest or concern is not addressed by the previously established entities.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_affairs_rankings">Student affairs rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Student affairs rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>
