     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government">Student government</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Student government">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UFSG.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/UFSG.png/180px-UFSG.png" width="180" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/56/UFSG.png/270px-UFSG.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/56/UFSG.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UFSG.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Seal for the UF Student Government
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida <a href="/wiki/Student_Government" title="Student Government" class="mw-redirect">Student Government</a> is the governing body of students who attend the University of Florida, representing the university's more than 50,000 undergraduate, graduate and professional students. The university's student government currently operates on a yearly $17.8 million dollar budget, one of the largest student government budgets in the United States, and is decided by a Legislative Senate Budget Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The student government was established in 1909 and consists of executive, judicial and unicameral legislative branches. The executive branch includes the student government president, vice president and treasurer elected by the student body during the spring semester, as well as nine agencies and forty-one cabinet members.</p> 
     <p>The student senate is the legislative branch, and is composed of 100 senators who serve one-year terms. The student body elects fifty senators during each spring semester and the remaining fifty during the fall semester. The senators elect a senate president and senate President pro tempore twice a year, after each semester's elections, to lead the student senate. During student government elections students may also vote on referendums, such as the renewable energy referendum,<sup id="cite_ref-Gators_for_a_Sustainable_Campus_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gators_for_a_Sustainable_Campus-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> which was approved by 78% of voting students in the spring of 2007. This referendum proposed a fifty-cents-per-credit-hour increase to student activity fees to fund renewable energy and efficiency on campus.</p> 
     <p>The student government judicial branch has three major components: the student supreme court (headed by a chief justice), the student honor court (headed by the honor court chancellor elected each spring), and the student traffic court (headed by a chief justice). The supreme court consists of five second or third-year law students nominated by the student government president and confirmed by the student senate. Each justice serves a &quot;life-time&quot; term, which extends through the individual justice's graduation and insulates the court from the politics of student government. The chief justice may appoint a marshal and clerk. The election commission, which listens and adjudicates all student government election complaints, is also part of the judicial branch. The commission includes 6 members, one of whom also serves as the commission chairman.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alma_Mater">Alma Mater</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Alma Mater">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater_(song)" title="Alma Mater (song)" class="mw-redirect">Alma Mater</a> for the University of Florida was composed by Milton Yeats in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_.26_area_transportation">Campus &amp; area transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Campus &amp; area transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The UF campus is served by nine bus routes of the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville_Regional_Transit_System" title="Gainesville Regional Transit System">Gainesville Regional Transit System</a> (RTS), which had over ten million riders in 2011. Students, faculty, and staff with university-issued ID cards are able to use the system at no extra cost. The RTS also provides other campus services, including Gator Aider (during football games) and Later Gator nighttime service.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>University of Florida is also served by the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville_Regional_Airport" title="Gainesville Regional Airport">Gainesville Regional Airport</a>, which is located in the Northeast portion of <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a> and has daily services to <a href="/wiki/Miami,_Florida" title="Miami, Florida" class="mw-redirect">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia" class="mw-redirect">Atlanta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WUFT.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/WUFT.jpg/150px-WUFT.jpg" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/WUFT.jpg/225px-WUFT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/WUFT.jpg/300px-WUFT.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WUFT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/WUFT_(TV)" title="WUFT (TV)">WUFT</a> studio on campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida community includes six major student-run media outlets.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/The_Independent_Florida_Alligator" title="The Independent Florida Alligator">The Independent Florida Alligator</a> is the largest <a href="/wiki/Student_newspaper" title="Student newspaper">student-run newspaper</a> in the United States, and operates without oversight from the university administration.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/WRUF_(AM)" title="WRUF (AM)">WRUF</a> (850 AM) features a mixture of local and syndicated talk programs, award-winning student-produced newscasts and sports talk shows, plus religious programming on Sunday mornings.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/WRUF-FM" title="WRUF-FM">WRUF-FM</a> (103.7 FM) broadcasts Country music and attracts an audience from the <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocala,_Florida" title="Ocala, Florida">Ocala</a> areas.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/WRUF-LD" title="WRUF-LD">WRUF-LD</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Low-power_broadcasting" title="Low-power broadcasting">low-power</a> television station that carries weather, news, and sports programming.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/WUFT_(TV)" title="WUFT (TV)">WUFT</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service" class="mw-redirect">PBS member</a> station with a variety of programming that includes a daily student-produced newscast.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/WUFT-FM" title="WUFT-FM">WUFT-FM</a> (89.1 FM) is an NPR member radio station which airs news and public affairs programming, including student-produced long-form news reporting. WUFT-FM's programming also airs on WJUF-FM (90.1).</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Various other journals and magazines are published by the university's academic units and student groups, including the literary journal <i><a href="/wiki/Subtropics_(journal)" title="Subtropics (journal)">Subtropics</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_placement">Career placement</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Career placement">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Florida Career Resource Center is located in the <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Student_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Student Union" class="mw-redirect">Reitz Student Union</a>. Its mission is to assist students and alumni who are seeking career development, career experiences, and employment opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> These services involve on and off-campus job interviews, career planning, assistance in applying to graduate and professional schools, and internship and co-op placements.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> The Career Resource Center offers workshops, information sessions, career fairs, and advisement on future career options. Staff also counsel students and alumni regarding resumes and portfolios, interviewing tactics, cover letters, job strategies and other potential leads for finding employment in the corporate, academic and government sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a> ranked the Career Resource Center as the best among 368 ranked universities in career and job placement services in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-princetonreview.com_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princetonreview.com-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> and fourth overall in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-princetonreview.com_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princetonreview.com-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF_HarnMuseum.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/150px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/225px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/UF_HarnMuseum.JPG/300px-UF_HarnMuseum.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UF_HarnMuseum.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Harn Museum of Art</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/150px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/225px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg/300px-UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UF_FloridaMuseumOfNaturalHistory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Florida_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Florida Museum of Natural History">Museum of Natural History</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Florida Museum of Natural History">Florida Museum of Natural History</a>, established in 1891, is one of the oldest natural history museums in the country and was officially chartered by the State of <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> This facility is dedicated to understanding, preserving and interpreting biological diversity and cultural heritage. In over 100 years of operations the Florida Museum of Natural History has been housed in several buildings, from the <a href="/wiki/Seagle_Building" title="Seagle Building">Seagle Building</a> to facilities at Dickinson Hall, Powell Hall, and the Randell Research Center. In 2000 the McGuire Center for Lepidoptera and Biodiversity was opened after a generous donation from University of Florida benefactors.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The McGuire Center houses a collection of more than six million butterfly and moth specimens, making it one of the largest collections of <a href="/wiki/Lepidoptera" title="Lepidoptera">Lepidoptera</a> in the world, rivaling that of the <a href="/wiki/Natural_History_Museum,_London" title="Natural History Museum, London">Natural History Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/London,_England" title="London, England" class="mw-redirect">London, England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Samuel_P._Harn_Museum_of_Art" title="Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art">Samuel P. Harn Museum of Art</a>, established in 1990, is also located at the University of Florida on the southwest part of campus.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> This facility is one of the largest university art museums in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">South</a>, the Harn has more than 7,000 works in its <a href="/wiki/Collection_(museum)" title="Collection (museum)" class="mw-redirect">permanent collection</a> and an array of temporary exhibitions. The museum's permanent collections are focused on <a href="/wiki/Asian_art" title="Asian art">Asian</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_art" title="African art">African</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">photography</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The university sponsors educational programs at the museum including films, lectures, interactive activities, and school and family offerings. In October 2005 the Harn expanded by more than 18,000 square feet (1,700&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) with the opening of the Mary Ann Harn Cofrin Pavilion, which includes new educational and meeting areas and the Camellia Court Cafe, the first eatery for visitors of the Cultural Plaza.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts_and_music">Performing arts and music</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Performing arts and music">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UF_Phillips_Center.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/150px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG" width="150" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/225px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/UF_Phillips_Center.JPG/300px-UF_Phillips_Center.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UF_Phillips_Center.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">Performing arts</a> venues at the University of Florida consist of the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constans_Theatre" title="Constans Theatre">Constans Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Baughman_Center" title="Baughman Center">Baughman Center</a>, and performances at the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> The mission is to provide an unparalleled experience where the performing artists create and share knowledge to serve the student body, faculty, and staff at the university; Gainesville residents; and visitors to North Central Florida.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a> was founded in the mid-1920s and is home to the Anderson Memorial Organ. The auditorium has a concert stage and can seat up to 843 patrons. The venue is suitable for <a href="/wiki/Concert" title="Concert">musical concerts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lecture" title="Lecture">special lectures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocations</a>, dance concerts, and pageants.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityAuditorium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/150px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg" width="150" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/225px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/UniversityAuditorium.jpg/300px-UniversityAuditorium.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityAuditorium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/University_Auditorium_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="University Auditorium (Gainesville, Florida)">University Auditorium</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Curtis_M._Phillips_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Curtis M. Phillips Center for the Performing Arts">Phillips Center for the Performing Arts</a> was founded in 1992 and is a performing arts <a href="/wiki/Theatre" title="Theatre">theatre</a>. The Phillips Center is located on the western side of campus, and hosts established and emerging national and international artists on the main stage, as well as the annual <a href="/wiki/Miss_University_of_Florida" title="Miss University of Florida">Miss University of Florida</a> pageant. In all, the Phillips Center consists of a 1,700-seat <a href="/wiki/Proscenium" title="Proscenium">proscenium hall</a> and the 200-seat Squitieri Studio Theatre.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Constans_Theatre" title="Constans Theatre">Constans Theatre</a> was founded in 1967 and is a performing arts venue located next to the <a href="/wiki/J._Wayne_Reitz_Union" title="J. Wayne Reitz Union">J. Wayne Reitz Union</a>. Constans Theatre serves as a venue for musical concerts, theater, dance, and lectures, and is a sub-venue of the Nadine McGuire Pavilion and Dance Pavilion.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Baughman_Center" title="Baughman Center">Baughman Center</a> was founded in 2000 and serves as a venue for small musical and performing arts events. The facility consists of two buildings located next to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Alice_(Gainesville,_Florida)" title="Lake Alice (Gainesville, Florida)">Lake Alice</a> on the western portion of campus. The main building is a 1,500-square-foot (140&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) pavilion, while the other is a 1,000-square-foot (93&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) administrative building. Overall the Baughman Center can accommodate up to 96 patrons.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_in_popular_culture" title="University of Florida in popular culture">University of Florida in popular culture</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida has been portrayed in several films, books, and television shows. In addition, the University of Florida campus has been the backdrop for a number of different movies, books, and even a song by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Petty_and_the_Heartbreakers" title="Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers">Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers</a>.</p> 
     <p>The University of Florida has been portrayed in a variety of television shows and motion pictures. Fictional UF alumni and faculty include Kevin Lomax and Mary Ann Lomax who were characters in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Devil%27s_Advocate_(1997_film)" title="The Devil's Advocate (1997 film)">The Devil's Advocate</a></i>. In the film <i><a href="/wiki/Days_of_Thunder" title="Days of Thunder">Days of Thunder</a></i>, the character Harry Hogge can be seen wearing a University of Florida ballcap. In the film <i><a href="/wiki/Deuce_Bigalow:_European_Gigolo" title="Deuce Bigalow: European Gigolo">Deuce Bigalow: European Gigolo</a></i>, a side character named Earl McManus is shown wearing a <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a> hat. The politician <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ritchie_(TV_character)" title="Robert Ritchie (TV character)" class="mw-redirect">Robert Ritchie</a> from the show <i><a href="/wiki/The_West_Wing" title="The West Wing">The West Wing</a></i> was a graduate of the university. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Morrison" title="Jim Morrison">Jim Morrison</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Doors_(film)" title="The Doors (film)">The Doors</a></i> was incorrectly portrayed as former University of Florida student. The film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hawk_is_Dying" title="The Hawk is Dying" class="mw-redirect">The Hawk is Dying</a></i> is based on the professor <a href="/wiki/Harry_Crews" title="Harry Crews">Harry Crews</a>, who served as a faculty member for the university. In the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_Vice" title="Miami Vice">Miami Vice</a></i> the protagonist <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Crockett" title="Sonny Crockett">Sonny Crockett</a> had played for the football team.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Robert_Cade" title="Robert Cade">Robert Cade</a>, a professor at the university's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Florida College of Medicine">College of Medicine</a>, invented the ubiquitous sports drink <a href="/wiki/Gatorade" title="Gatorade">Gatorade</a> as a hydration supplement for the Florida Gators football team in 1965–66. A series of Gatorade television commercials, &quot;The Legend of Gatorade,&quot; prominently featured the university and the Gators.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Athletic_Association" title="University of Florida Athletic Association">University of Florida Athletic Association</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida's intercollegiate sports teams, known as the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators" title="Florida Gators">Florida Gators</a>&quot;, compete in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> For the 2009–10 school year, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Athletic_Association" title="University of Florida Athletic Association">University Athletic Association</a> budgeted more $85 million for its sports teams and facilities. Since 1986, the Gators have won twenty-three of the last twenty-six SEC All-Sports Trophies, recognizing Florida as the best overall athletics program in the SEC.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> Florida's sports program has ranked among the top five in the nation in twenty of the past twenty-eight years, and it is the only Division I program that has ranked among the top ten athletic programs in the country in each of the last twenty-eight years.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Florida has won a total of thirty-one team national championships,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> twenty-six of which are NCAA championships.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Florida is one of only two Division I FBS universities to win multiple national championships in each of the two most popular NCAA sports: football (1996, 2006, 2008) and men's basketball (2006, 2007).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_Olympians" title="List of University of Florida Olympians">List of University of Florida Olympians</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida has a long history of producing athletes who compete in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>. Over 150 Gator athletes from over thirty different countries have competed in the Games, winning forty-four Olympic <a href="/wiki/Gold_medals" title="Gold medals" class="mw-redirect">gold medals</a>, twenty-three <a href="/wiki/Silver_medals" title="Silver medals" class="mw-redirect">silver medals</a> and twenty-three <a href="/wiki/Bronze_medals" title="Bronze medals" class="mw-redirect">bronze medals</a> through the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> The list of University of Florida alumni who are Olympic gold medalists includes sprinters <a href="/wiki/Kerron_Clement" title="Kerron Clement">Kerron Clement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mitchell" title="Dennis Mitchell">Dennis Mitchell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Williams_(athlete)" title="Bernard Williams (athlete)">Bernard Williams</a>; marathon runner <a href="/wiki/Frank_Shorter" title="Frank Shorter">Frank Shorter</a>; baseball outfielder <a href="/wiki/Brad_Wilkerson" title="Brad Wilkerson">Brad Wilkerson</a>; basketball forward <a href="/wiki/DeLisha_Milton-Jones" title="DeLisha Milton-Jones">DeLisha Milton-Jones</a>; soccer players <a href="/wiki/Heather_Mitts" title="Heather Mitts">Heather Mitts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abby_Wambach" title="Abby Wambach">Abby Wambach</a>; and swimmers <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Caulkins" title="Tracy Caulkins">Tracy Caulkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Haislett" title="Nicole Haislett">Nicole Haislett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Lochte" title="Ryan Lochte">Ryan Lochte</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dara_Torres" title="Dara Torres">Dara Torres</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida Gators football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg/250px-Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg" width="250" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg/375px-Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg/500px-Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Dsg_UF_Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium_Inside_20050507.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Interior of 
        <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, also known as &quot;The Swamp.&quot;
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida fielded its first official varsity football team in the fall of 1906, when the university held its first classes on its new Gainesville campus. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_football" title="Florida Gators football">Florida Gators football</a> team has played in thirty-seven bowl games, won three consensus national championships and eight <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Conference" title="Southeastern Conference">Southeastern Conference</a> (SEC) championships, produced 135 All-Americans, thirty-five <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) first-round draft choices, and three <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> winners.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Gators won their first post-season game on Christmas Day 1912 in the <a href="/wiki/Bacardi_Bowl" title="Bacardi Bowl">Bacardi Bowl</a>, beating the Vedado Athletic Club 28–0 in <a href="/wiki/Havana,_Cuba" title="Havana, Cuba" class="mw-redirect">Havana, Cuba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> The Gators earned national attention in 1928, setting a national record for most points scored in a season by an 8–1 team that also produced the Gators' first <a href="/wiki/All-American" title="All-American" class="mw-redirect">All-American</a>, end <a href="/wiki/Dale_Van_Sickel" title="Dale Van Sickel">Dale Van Sickel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gatorfootballPDF_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatorfootballPDF-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> The Gators' first major bowl win was the 1967 <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl_(game)" title="Orange Bowl (game)" class="mw-redirect">Orange Bowl</a> in which coach <a href="/wiki/Ray_Graves" title="Ray Graves">Ray Graves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> quarterback <a href="/wiki/Steve_Spurrier" title="Steve Spurrier">Steve Spurrier</a> led the Gators to a 27–12 victory over the <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Tech_Yellow_Jackets_football" title="Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets football">Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1990, Spurrier returned to his <a href="/wiki/Alma_mater" title="Alma mater">alma mater</a> as its new head coach, and spurred the Gators to their first six official SEC football championships. The Gators, quarterbacked by their second Heisman Trophy winner, <a href="/wiki/Danny_Wuerffel" title="Danny Wuerffel">Danny Wuerffel</a>, won their first national championship in 1996 with a 52–20 victory over <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_Seminoles_football" title="Florida State Seminoles football">Florida State Seminoles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Bowl" title="Sugar Bowl">Sugar Bowl</a>. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Urban_Meyer" title="Urban Meyer">Urban Meyer</a> coached the Gators to a 13–1 record, capturing their seventh <a href="/wiki/SEC_Championship" title="SEC Championship" class="mw-redirect">SEC Championship</a>, and defeating the top-ranked <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_football" title="Ohio State Buckeyes football">Ohio State Buckeyes</a> 41–14 for the <a href="/wiki/BCS_National_Championship" title="BCS National Championship" class="mw-redirect">BCS National Championship</a>. In 2008, the Gators' third Heisman-winning quarterback, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Tebow" title="Tim Tebow">Tim Tebow</a>, led them in a 24–14 <a href="/wiki/BCS_Championship_Game" title="BCS Championship Game" class="mw-redirect">BCS Championship Game</a> victory over the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Sooners_football" title="Oklahoma Sooners football">Oklahoma Sooners</a> for their third national championship.</p> 
     <p>Since 1930, the Gators' home field has been <a href="/wiki/Ben_Hill_Griffin_Stadium" title="Ben Hill Griffin Stadium">Ben Hill Griffin Stadium</a>, which seats over 90,000 fans—the twelfth largest college football venue in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> The stadium is popularly known as &quot;The Swamp&quot;, and <i>The Sporting News</i> has named Florida's fans as the top college crowd in the nation and ranked the stadium as the nation's loudest.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_men%27s_basketball" title="Florida Gators men's basketball">Florida Gators men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:O%27Connell_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/200px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/300px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/O%27Connell_Center.jpg/400px-O%27Connell_Center.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:O%27Connell_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Interior view of the 
        <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>, configured for basketball.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gators_men%27s_basketball" title="Florida Gators men's basketball">Florida Gators men's basketball</a> team has also gained national recognition over the past twenty years.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> The Gators went to the <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> of the 1994 NCAA tournament under coach <a href="/wiki/Lon_Kruger" title="Lon Kruger">Lon Kruger</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> and coach <a href="/wiki/Billy_Donovan" title="Billy Donovan">Billy Donovan</a> led the Gators back to the NCAA Final Four in 2000, losing to the <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="Michigan State Spartans men's basketball">Michigan State Spartans</a> in the final. Under Donovan, the Gators won their first Southeastern Conference (SEC) tournament championship in 2005, beating the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Kentucky Wildcats men's basketball">Kentucky Wildcats</a>. After repeating as SEC tournament champions in 2006, the Gators won their first basketball national championship, defeating the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">UCLA Bruins</a> 73–57 in the final game of the NCAA basketball tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Gators beat the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_Razorbacks_men%27s_basketball" title="Arkansas Razorbacks men's basketball">Arkansas Razorbacks</a> 77–56 to win their third consecutive SEC tournament title in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Florida defeated Ohio State 84–75 to again win the NCAA basketball tournament championship, becoming the first team to win back-to-back national championships with the same starting line-up.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Gators play their home games in the <a href="/wiki/O%27Connell_Center" title="O'Connell Center">O'Connell Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> The 12,000-seat multi-purpose indoor arena was completed in 1980, and is popularly known as the &quot;O'Dome.&quot;</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_people" title="List of University of Florida people">List of University of Florida people</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Alumni_Association" title="University of Florida Alumni Association">University of Florida Alumni Association</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Florida has more than 330,000 alumni. In total 57,000 are dues-paying members of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Alumni_Association" title="University of Florida Alumni Association">University of Florida Alumni Association</a>. Florida alumni can be found in every state and more than 100 foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Florida alumni account for multiple <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners, ten <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. Senators</a>, forty <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">U.S. Representatives</a>, eleven <a href="/wiki/Governor_(United_States)" title="Governor (United States)">state governors</a>, and eight <a href="/wiki/Ambassadors_of_the_United_States" title="Ambassadors of the United States">U.S. ambassadors</a>, multiple state supreme court judges, and various federal courts judges. Florida graduates have served as the executive leaders of such diverse institutions as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">United States Marine Corps</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Organization_for_Women" title="National Organization for Women">National Organization for Women</a>.</p> 
     <p><br /></p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty">Notable faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Notable faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Florida_faculty_and_administrators" title="List of University of Florida faculty and administrators">List of University of Florida faculty and administrators</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Individual awards won by UF faculty include a <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>, numerous <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prizes" title="Pulitzer Prizes" class="mw-redirect">Pulitzer Prizes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s top award for research and Smithsonian Institution's conservation award.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> There are currently more than 60 Eminent Scholar chairs, and nearly 60 faculty elections to the National Academy of Sciences, Engineering, or Arts and Sciences, the Institute of Medicine or a counterpart in a foreign nation. More than two dozen faculty are members of the National Academies of Science and Engineering and the Institute of Medicine or counterpart in a foreign nation.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaGuide_105-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaGuide-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="University_benefactors">University benefactors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Florida&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: University benefactors">edit</a>]</span></h2>

      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida_Investment_Corporation" title="University of Florida Investment Corporation">University of Florida Investment Corporation</a>

The name, the &quot;University of Florida,&quot; has been held by three separate schools: the <a href="/wiki/West_Florida_Seminary" title="West Florida Seminary" class="mw-redirect">West Florida Seminary</a> was renamed the &quot;University of Florida&quot; by the legislature, and held the name from 1883 to 1902; Florida Agricultural College was renamed in 1902 and held the name until 1905; and the name of the new University of the State of Florida was simplified to the University of Florida in 1909. The West Florida Seminary was a predecessor to the modern <a href="/wiki/Florida_State_University" title="Florida State University">Florida State University</a> in Tallahassee.</span></li>
